<p><i><b>Overexposed</b></i> is the fourth studio album by the American band <a href="/wiki/Maroon_5" title="Maroon 5">Maroon 5</a>, released on June 20, 2012, by <a href="/wiki/A%26M_Octone_Records" title="A&amp;M Octone Records">A&amp;M Octone Records</a>. The album was recorded between 2011 and 2012 and was driven after the moderate success of their third album, <i><a href="/wiki/Hands_All_Over_(album)" title="Hands All Over (album)">Hands All Over</a></i> (2010), and later by the enormous success of the re-released edition, which was promoted by the single "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Moves_Like_Jagger" title="Moves Like Jagger">Moves Like Jagger</a>", recorded as a collaboration with <a href="/wiki/Christina_Aguilera" title="Christina Aguilera">Christina Aguilera</a>. It is the band's only album not to feature keyboardist, rhythm guitarist and background vocalist, <a href="/wiki/Jesse_Carmichael" title="Jesse Carmichael">Jesse Carmichael</a>, who took a temporary break from performing with the group to focus on his studies back then, but eventually returned to Maroon 5 in 2014. The band worked with different producers, such as <a href="/wiki/Max_Martin" title="Max Martin">Max Martin</a>, who serves as the album's executive producer, <a href="/wiki/Ryan_Tedder" title="Ryan Tedder">Ryan Tedder</a>, <a href="/wiki/Shellback_(record_producer)" title="Shellback (record producer)">Shellback</a> and <a href="/wiki/Benny_Blanco" title="Benny Blanco">Benny Blanco</a>. The band's guitarist and Levine's usual co-writer <a href="/wiki/James_Valentine_(musician)" title="James Valentine (musician)">James Valentine</a> only has four credits on the album.</p>
<p>The accompanying artwork, created by LA artist <a href="/wiki/Young_%26_Sick" title="Young &amp; Sick">Young &amp; Sick</a>, is a colorful collage of illustrations seemingly inspired by the likes of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Picasso" title="Picasso">Picasso</a> and a range of modern cartoonists. Its title is a smirking allusion to Levine's ubiquity, while its sound is a reflection of how the group wishes to retain the large audience they won once again with "Moves Like Jagger". The album's lead single "<a href="/wiki/Payphone_(song)" title="Payphone (song)">Payphone</a>", featuring rapper <a href="/wiki/Wiz_Khalifa" title="Wiz Khalifa">Wiz Khalifa</a>, produced by Shellback and Benny Blanco, was released and performed on <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Voice_(U.S.)" title="The Voice (U.S.)">The Voice</a></i> on April 16, 2012. The song was a success, reaching number two on the <a href="/wiki/Billboard_Hot_100" title="Billboard Hot 100"><i>Billboard</i> Hot 100</a> chart, as well as on the <a href="/wiki/ARIA_Charts" title="ARIA Charts">ARIA Charts</a>, while it topped the <a href="/wiki/UK_Singles_Chart" title="UK Singles Chart">UK Singles Chart</a>, <a href="/wiki/Canadian_Hot_100" title="Canadian Hot 100">Canadian Hot 100</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Federation_of_the_Italian_Music_Industry" title="Federation of the Italian Music Industry">Italian Singles Chart</a>. The second single, "<a href="/wiki/One_More_Night_(Maroon_5_song)" title="One More Night (Maroon 5 song)">One More Night</a>", was released on June 19, 2012. The song topped the <i>Billboard</i> Hot 100 for nine weeks, becoming their longest Hot 100 reign. All four singles released from <i>Overexposed</i> have reached the Hot 100 top-ten, including the last two of them: "<a href="/wiki/Daylight_(Maroon_5_song)" title="Daylight (Maroon 5 song)">Daylight</a>" and "<a href="/wiki/Love_Somebody_(Maroon_5_song)" title="Love Somebody (Maroon 5 song)">Love Somebody</a>".</p>
<p>The album received a mixed reception from <a href="/wiki/Music_journalism" title="Music journalism">music critics</a>. Some praised the album, calling it their strongest effort, but others criticized the direction the band decided to take, calling it a failed attempt to go mainstream. Additionally, critics and fans alike perceived the album as overly focused on Levine. It debuted at number 2 on the <a href="/wiki/UK_Albums_Chart" title="UK Albums Chart">UK Albums Chart</a>, selling 38,000 copies, and on the <a href="/wiki/Billboard_200" title="Billboard 200">US <i>Billboard</i> 200</a> chart, selling 222,000 copies. According to the <a href="/wiki/International_Federation_of_the_Phonographic_Industry" title="International Federation of the Phonographic Industry">International Federation of the Phonographic Industry</a> (IFPI), <i>Overexposed</i> was the 10th global best-selling album of 2012 with sales of 2.2 million copies,and sold approximately 3 million copies due to 2013.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wwsales_1-0"><a href="#cite_note-wwsales-1">[1]</a></sup> To promote the album, the band started the <a href="/wiki/Overexposed_Tour" title="Overexposed Tour">Overexposed Tour</a>, which lasted from 2012 to 2014.</p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Background">Background</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Overexposed_(album)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Background">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:AdamLevine2011.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="4271" data-file-width="3142" height="231" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/AdamLevine2011.jpg/170px-AdamLevine2011.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/AdamLevine2011.jpg/255px-AdamLevine2011.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/AdamLevine2011.jpg/340px-AdamLevine2011.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:AdamLevine2011.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
According to <a href="/wiki/Adam_Levine" title="Adam Levine">Adam Levine</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/Hands_All_Over_(album)" title="Hands All Over (album)">Hands All Over</a></i> experienced moderate commercial success because of its sound and the location in which it was recorded (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vevey,_Switzerland" title="Vevey, Switzerland">Vevey, Switzerland</a>).</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In September 2010, the band released their third studio album, <i><a href="/wiki/Hands_All_Over_(album)" title="Hands All Over (album)">Hands All Over</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HAO_Info_2-0"><a href="#cite_note-HAO_Info-2">[2]</a></sup> While preparing the album, the band received a phone call from <a href="/wiki/Robert_John_%22Mutt%22_Lange" title='Robert John "Mutt" Lange'>Robert John "Mutt" Lange</a>, who had heard the band were beginning to write a new record, and expressed an interest in producing it.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HAO_Info_2-1"><a href="#cite_note-HAO_Info-2">[2]</a></sup> The album received generally favorable reviews from <a href="/wiki/Music_journalism" title="Music journalism">music critics</a> and debuted at number two on the US <a href="/wiki/Billboard_200" title="Billboard 200"><i>Billboard</i> 200</a> chart.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Metacritic_3-0"><a href="#cite_note-Metacritic-3">[3]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-US-albums_4-0"><a href="#cite_note-US-albums-4">[4]</a></sup> However, the album experienced moderate success in overall sales; regarding that, the band guitarist <a href="/wiki/James_Valentine_(musician)" title="James Valentine (musician)">James Valentine</a> expressed some frustration and said that a new album may be coming sooner than was originally planned.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-billboardinterview_5-0"><a href="#cite_note-billboardinterview-5">[5]</a></sup> Valentine further commented:</p>
<blockquote>
<p>"It would be nice to start working on another record next year". "I think with the last two records, it's been a little bit unbalanced, in that we had so much success and there was so much of the world to cover that our studio/road balance was a little off... In a perfect world we'd tour for six months and maybe record for six months, but that's not the way it works. But the whole point is to make more music, and if anything you can spend too much time out there."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-billboardinterview_5-1"><a href="#cite_note-billboardinterview-5">[5]</a></sup></p>
</blockquote>
<p>Valentine also said the band has "tons of material" available, including holdovers including songs from <i>Hands All Over</i> and also other tracks the band has written since then. "I think everybody's been pretty busy compiling ideas for the next one," he stated. "With technology and the recording capacity we have on our laptops, we can be a little more prolific while we're [touring]. We've never been able to do that before. I think we could go in and make a record today and have a pretty solid album."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-billboardinterview_5-2"><a href="#cite_note-billboardinterview-5">[5]</a></sup> In July 2011, the band re-released <i>Hands All Over</i> and included a new song called "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Moves_Like_Jagger" title="Moves Like Jagger">Moves Like Jagger</a>" which featured American recording artist <a href="/wiki/Christina_Aguilera" title="Christina Aguilera">Christina Aguilera</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup> The song enjoyed a massive commercial success reaching number one on over <a href="/wiki/Moves_like_Jagger#Charts" title="Moves like Jagger">22 national singles chart</a> including on the US <a href="/wiki/Billboard_Hot_100" title="Billboard Hot 100"><i>Billboard</i> Hot 100</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup> In an interview with Mike Wood of <i><a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_Times" title="Los Angeles Times">Los Angeles Times</a></i>, Levine explained what went wrong on <i>Hands All Over</i>, "I don't think we knew what kind of record we were making. It was such a hodgepodge — all these disparate ideas and songs that didn't make any sense together. He also stated, "We were in this idyllic paradise, which is a horrible place to make a record. <a href="/wiki/Switzerland" title="Switzerland">Switzerland</a>'s neutrality is very famous, and I feel like that neutrality infected Maroon 5's third album".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-latimes_8-0"><a href="#cite_note-latimes-8">[8]</a></sup> Levine further stated that "Moves Like Jagger" saved them and totally revived the group.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-latimes_8-1"><a href="#cite_note-latimes-8">[8]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Recording_and_production">Recording and production</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Overexposed_(album)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Recording and production">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ryan_Tedder_OneRepublic_Austria_3.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="4272" data-file-width="2848" height="255" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/Ryan_Tedder_OneRepublic_Austria_3.jpg/170px-Ryan_Tedder_OneRepublic_Austria_3.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/Ryan_Tedder_OneRepublic_Austria_3.jpg/255px-Ryan_Tedder_OneRepublic_Austria_3.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/Ryan_Tedder_OneRepublic_Austria_3.jpg/340px-Ryan_Tedder_OneRepublic_Austria_3.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Ryan_Tedder_OneRepublic_Austria_3.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
According to <a href="/wiki/Ryan_Tedder" title="Ryan Tedder">Ryan Tedder</a>, <i>Overexposed</i> contains a fresh sound.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The band started writing songs for <i>Overexposed</i> during their latest tour in support of <i>Hands All Over</i>. After concluding with the tour, the band recorded the material of the album at the Conway Recording Studios located in <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles" title="Los Angeles">Los Angeles</a>, <a href="/wiki/California" title="California">California</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-latimes_8-2"><a href="#cite_note-latimes-8">[8]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-announcement_9-0"><a href="#cite_note-announcement-9">[9]</a></sup> On March 22, 2012, the band posted a video on <a href="/wiki/YouTube" title="YouTube">YouTube</a> featuring numerous scenes from the band in the studio, recording the album.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup> Speaking about the development on the material, Valentine revealed that "Moves Like Jagger" was the first time the band worked with an outside writer, so they decided to implement it more on <i>Overexposed</i>. "At this point in our career I think it was a good thing to completely mix up our process and it yielded good results, as well as a more collaborative spirit within the band. We wanted to make something that sounded contemporary with the elements of a lot of early eras of pop music" explained Valentine.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rollingstone_11-0"><a href="#cite_note-rollingstone-11">[11]</a></sup> On the development of the album, Levine also commented, "<i>Overexposed</i> is definitely our most diverse and poppiest album yet. We had a great time recording it. I can't wait for our fans to hear the record, as well as hitting the road to play it live for everyone later this year."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-announcement_9-1"><a href="#cite_note-announcement-9">[9]</a></sup> In another interview for <i><a href="/wiki/Rolling_Stone" title="Rolling Stone">Rolling Stone</a></i>, the singer revealed that is their most dance-driven album ever, commenting: "It's very much an old-fashioned disco tune. I have a love/hate relationship with it – but mostly I love it."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rs_12-0"><a href="#cite_note-rs-12">[12]</a></sup></p>
<p>The album was executively produced by <a href="/wiki/Max_Martin" title="Max Martin">Max Martin</a>, with additional tracks produced by <a href="/wiki/Benny_Blanco" title="Benny Blanco">Benny Blanco</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ryan_Tedder" title="Ryan Tedder">Ryan Tedder</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-announcement_9-2"><a href="#cite_note-announcement-9">[9]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-billboard2_13-0"><a href="#cite_note-billboard2-13">[13]</a></sup> Tedder commented that the sound of the songs was very fresh and would affect kids. However, he further stated, "maintaining that interest — that's the hardest thing in the world."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-latimes_8-3"><a href="#cite_note-latimes-8">[8]</a></sup> Blanco explained that he and Levine first met during recording the song "<a href="/wiki/Stereo_Hearts" title="Stereo Hearts">Stereo Hearts</a>" by <a href="/wiki/Gym_Class_Heroes" title="Gym Class Heroes">Gym Class Heroes</a> on which Levine is featured.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-latimes_8-4"><a href="#cite_note-latimes-8">[8]</a></sup> The producer explained that when Levine heard the song he solely wanted in for himself on which Blanco responded that they will make another track for the band.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-latimes_8-5"><a href="#cite_note-latimes-8">[8]</a></sup> After producing "Moves Like Jagger", he also worked on <i>Overexposed</i> and produced some songs including the <a href="/wiki/Lead_single" title="Lead single">lead single</a> of the album, "<a href="/wiki/Payphone_(song)" title="Payphone (song)">Payphone</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-latimes_8-6"><a href="#cite_note-latimes-8">[8]</a></sup> Although new collaborators were recruited to help developing the album, Levine wrote all the songs with additional help from Valentine and produced a large portion of it, including the ballad "<a href="/wiki/Sad_(Maroon_5_song)" title="Sad (Maroon 5 song)">Sad</a>". According to Valentine, the development of the song began one morning, when he woke up and "before he was even awake" he was at his living room's piano playing the melody.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-valentine_14-0"><a href="#cite_note-valentine-14">[14]</a></sup> For an interview with <a href="/wiki/MTV_News" title="MTV News">MTV News</a>, Levine told that "Sad" is his most personal track on the album, but didn't reveal the inspiration behind it,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup> although <a href="/wiki/Music_journalism" title="Music journalism">critics</a> speculated it was inspired by the singer's break up with <a href="/wiki/Victoria%27s_Secret" title="Victoria's Secret">Victoria's Secret</a> model <a href="/wiki/Anne_Vyalitsyna" title="Anne Vyalitsyna">Anne Vyalitsyna</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sun_16-0"><a href="#cite_note-sun-16">[16]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Composition">Composition</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Overexposed_(album)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Composition">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Influence_and_sound">Influence and sound</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Overexposed_(album)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Influence and sound">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><i>Overexposed</i> is a <a href="/wiki/Pop_music" title="Pop music">pop</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-americansongwriter_17-0"><a href="#cite_note-americansongwriter-17">[17]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Pop_rock" title="Pop rock">pop rock</a> album<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ew_19-0"><a href="#cite_note-ew-19">[19]</a></sup> with <a href="/wiki/Dance-pop" title="Dance-pop">dance-pop</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-allmusic_20-0"><a href="#cite_note-allmusic-20">[20]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Disco" title="Disco">disco</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rollingstonereview_21-0"><a href="#cite_note-rollingstonereview-21">[21]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Electropop" title="Electropop">electropop</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-musicOMH_22-0"><a href="#cite_note-musicOMH-22">[22]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Contemporary_R%26B" title="Contemporary R&amp;B">R&amp;B</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-billboard_review_23-0"><a href="#cite_note-billboard_review-23">[23]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Reggae" title="Reggae">reggae</a> influences.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rs_12-1"><a href="#cite_note-rs-12">[12]</a></sup> According to the band's official website, the album is "a chock-full collection of undeniable, anthemic melodies."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-announcement_9-3"><a href="#cite_note-announcement-9">[9]</a></sup> Multiple critics stated that "Moves Like Jagger" served as the biggest influence for composing and writing most songs on <i>Overexposed</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ew_19-1"><a href="#cite_note-ew-19">[19]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-musicOMH_22-1"><a href="#cite_note-musicOMH-22">[22]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-guardian_24-0"><a href="#cite_note-guardian-24">[24]</a></sup> Additionally, they noted that the works by Barbadian recording artist <a href="/wiki/Rihanna" title="Rihanna">Rihanna</a> influenced the album's sound.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ew_19-2"><a href="#cite_note-ew-19">[19]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-musicOMH_22-2"><a href="#cite_note-musicOMH-22">[22]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Songs_and_lyrics">Songs and lyrics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Overexposed_(album)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Songs and lyrics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="mbox-small" role="presentation" style="border:1px solid #aaa;background-color:#f9f9f9;">
<tr>

<tr>
<td class="mbox-text" colspan="2" style="line-height:1.1em"><span><i>Problems playing this file? See <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Media_help" title="Wikipedia:Media help">media help</a>.</i></span></td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>The album's opening track, "<a href="/wiki/One_More_Night_(Maroon_5_song)" title="One More Night (Maroon 5 song)">One More Night</a>", is an "irresistible sexy reggae jam"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rs_12-2"><a href="#cite_note-rs-12">[12]</a></sup> that features influences of pop and <a href="/wiki/Rock_music" title="Rock music">rock</a> music.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-popcrush_26-0"><a href="#cite_note-popcrush-26">[26]</a></sup> Lyrically, the storyline follows or being able to untangle from the particular love interest.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-popcrush_26-1"><a href="#cite_note-popcrush-26">[26]</a></sup> The second track on the album, "Payphone" is a pop and R&amp;B song<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-billboard_review_23-1"><a href="#cite_note-billboard_review-23">[23]</a></sup> that contains <a href="/wiki/Hip_hop_music" title="Hip hop music">hip hop</a> beats and <a href="/wiki/Piano" title="Piano">piano</a> hooks.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-digital_spy_review_27-0"><a href="#cite_note-digital_spy_review-27">[27]</a></sup> Featuring a verse by American rapper <a href="/wiki/Wiz_Khalifa" title="Wiz Khalifa">Wiz Khalifa</a>, the song explores the way a relationship used to be in the past.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-popcrush2_28-0"><a href="#cite_note-popcrush2-28">[28]</a></sup> "<a href="/wiki/Daylight_(Maroon_5_song)" title="Daylight (Maroon 5 song)">Daylight</a>" is a <a href="/wiki/Soft_rock" title="Soft rock">soft rock</a> song,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-billboard.com_29-0"><a href="#cite_note-billboard.com-29">[29]</a></sup> that carries influence from the works of English band <a href="/wiki/Coldplay" title="Coldplay">Coldplay</a>. According to Adam Markovitz of <i><a href="/wiki/Entertainment_Weekly" title="Entertainment Weekly">Entertainment Weekly</a></i>, the song has <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Refrain_(song)" title="Refrain (song)">choruses</a> that are thickly produced and the only physical instrument that you can pick is Levine's <a href="/wiki/Larynx" title="Larynx">larynx</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ew_19-4"><a href="#cite_note-ew-19">[19]</a></sup> "<a href="/wiki/Lucky_Strike_(song)" title="Lucky Strike (song)">Lucky Strike</a>" is a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Funk_music" title="Funk music">funk</a> song<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ew_19-5"><a href="#cite_note-ew-19">[19]</a></sup> that features <a href="/wiki/Dubstep" title="Dubstep">dubstep</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Soul_rock" title="Soul rock">soul rock</a> influences<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-artistdirect_25-1"><a href="#cite_note-artistdirect-25">[25]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nmereview_30-0"><a href="#cite_note-nmereview-30">[30]</a></sup> and lyrically discovers the theme of <a href="/wiki/Sexual_intercourse" title="Sexual intercourse">sexual intercourse</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Plugged_In_31-0"><a href="#cite_note-Plugged_In-31">[31]</a></sup> The fifth track on the album, "<a href="/wiki/The_Man_Who_Never_Lied" title="The Man Who Never Lied">The Man Who Never Lied</a>," produced by <a href="/wiki/Brian_West_(musician)" title="Brian West (musician)">Brian West</a>, is a pop and pop rock song<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-star_pulse_32-0"><a href="#cite_note-star_pulse-32">[32]</a></sup> that finds the protagonist in a relationship trouble where he is playing the role of a good person.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-billboard.com_29-1"><a href="#cite_note-billboard.com-29">[29]</a></sup> According to Nate Chinen of <i><a href="/wiki/The_New_York_Times" title="The New York Times">The New York Times</a></i>, in the song, Levine sings "about spoiling his perfect record of honesty to spare a quarreling lover some hurtful feelings."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup> "<a href="/wiki/Love_Somebody_(Maroon_5_song)" title="Love Somebody (Maroon 5 song)">Love Somebody</a>" is the sixth track on the album; a dance-pop song<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-billboard.com_29-2"><a href="#cite_note-billboard.com-29">[29]</a></sup> it contains a <a href="/wiki/Sly_Stone" title="Sly Stone">Sly Stone</a>-meets-<a href="/wiki/Eurythmics" title="Eurythmics">Eurythmics</a> <a href="/wiki/Synthesizer" title="Synthesizer">synth</a> <a href="/wiki/Hook_(music)" title="Hook (music)">hook</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rollingstonereview_21-1"><a href="#cite_note-rollingstonereview-21">[21]</a></sup> The funk-laden<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-digitalspy_34-0"><a href="#cite_note-digitalspy-34">[34]</a></sup> seventh song, "Ladykiller" features a guitar solo<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bbcmusic_35-0"><a href="#cite_note-bbcmusic-35">[35]</a></sup> and an elastic <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Funk_music" title="Funk music">funk</a> groove, combined with Adam Levine's blue-eyed soul vocal and pleasing echoes of <a href="/wiki/Hall_%26_Oates" title="Hall &amp; Oates">Hall &amp; Oates</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-independent_36-0"><a href="#cite_note-independent-36">[36]</a></sup> It was inspired by the work of American recording artist <a href="/wiki/Michael_Jackson" title="Michael Jackson">Michael Jackson</a>, as noted by the reviewers of <a href="/wiki/BBC_Music" title="BBC Music">BBC Music</a> and <a href="/wiki/Virgin_Media" title="Virgin Media">Virgin Media</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bbcmusic_35-1"><a href="#cite_note-bbcmusic-35">[35]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-virgin_37-0"><a href="#cite_note-virgin-37">[37]</a></sup></p>
<table class="mbox-small-left" role="presentation" style="border:1px solid #aaa;background-color:#f9f9f9;float:left">

<div class="description" style="padding:2px 0 0 0">"<a href="/wiki/Sad_(Maroon_5_song)" title="Sad (Maroon 5 song)">Sad</a>" is a <a href="/wiki/Piano_ballad" title="Piano ballad">piano ballad</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-billboard.com_29-3"><a href="#cite_note-billboard.com-29">[29]</a></sup> which highlights Levine's soulful tone that his voice possesses.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RTE_38-0"><a href="#cite_note-RTE-38">[38]</a></sup> and is reminiscent of the works by <a href="/wiki/Adele" title="Adele">Adele</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nmereview_30-1"><a href="#cite_note-nmereview-30">[30]</a></sup></div>

</tr>
<tr>
<td class="mbox-text" colspan="2" style="line-height:1.1em"><span><i>Problems playing this file? See <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Media_help" title="Wikipedia:Media help">media help</a>.</i></span></td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>The eighth song on the album, "Fortune Teller" has a pop tempo piano beat, that meshes with the song to provide a mix of emotions. The song gives a sort of "I want you, but I can't decide for you" feel.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-billboard.com_29-4"><a href="#cite_note-billboard.com-29">[29]</a></sup> "<a href="/wiki/Sad_(Maroon_5_song)" title="Sad (Maroon 5 song)">Sad</a>" is a <a href="/wiki/Piano_ballad" title="Piano ballad">piano ballad</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-billboard.com_29-5"><a href="#cite_note-billboard.com-29">[29]</a></sup> which highlights Levine's soulful tone that his voice possesses.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RTE_38-1"><a href="#cite_note-RTE-38">[38]</a></sup> Nick Levine of <i><a href="/wiki/NME" title="NME">NME</a></i> labeled the song as "an <a href="/wiki/Adele" title="Adele">Adele</a>-apeing weepie".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nmereview_30-2"><a href="#cite_note-nmereview-30">[30]</a></sup> Lyrically, "Sad" is a song on which Levine "achingly" declares the end of his relationship and his heartbreak.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup> The tenth track "Tickets" features twisting production that "comes through as a tight, techno-influenced pop song".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-billboard.com_29-6"><a href="#cite_note-billboard.com-29">[29]</a></sup> According to a reviewer of <i><a href="/wiki/Billboard_(magazine)" title="Billboard (magazine)">Billboard</a></i>, the song is reminiscent of Maroon 5's 2010 single "<a href="/wiki/Give_a_Little_More" title="Give a Little More">Give a Little More</a>"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-billboard.com_29-7"><a href="#cite_note-billboard.com-29">[29]</a></sup> and it has lyrics about someone being a <a href="/wiki/Snob" title="Snob">snob</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ew_19-6"><a href="#cite_note-ew-19">[19]</a></sup> "<a href="/wiki/Doin%27_Dirt" title="Doin' Dirt">Doin' Dirt</a>" is a <a href="/wiki/Hi-NRG" title="Hi-NRG">high-energy</a>, beat-driven song,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-billboard.com_29-8"><a href="#cite_note-billboard.com-29">[29]</a></sup> and a "a revved, funky club cut".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rs_12-3"><a href="#cite_note-rs-12">[12]</a></sup> Its verses talk about "horndog rhapsodies", with lyrics such as: "I light you up when I get inside".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hampton_40-0"><a href="#cite_note-hampton-40">[40]</a></sup> The final track on the album, "Beautiful Goodbye" was described as a "rhythmic ballad."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rs_12-4"><a href="#cite_note-rs-12">[12]</a></sup> It's an acoustic ode that's bittersweet, but at the same time positive.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-billboard.com_29-9"><a href="#cite_note-billboard.com-29">[29]</a></sup> Additional three tracks are present on the deluxe edition of <i>Overexposed</i>, including "<a href="/wiki/Wipe_Your_Eyes" title="Wipe Your Eyes">Wipe Your Eyes</a>", "Wasted Years" and "<a href="/wiki/Kiss_(Prince_song)" title="Kiss (Prince song)">Kiss</a>", a cover of the 1986 single by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Prince_(singer)" title="Prince (singer)">Prince</a>. Wipe Your Eyes" is a mid-tempo piano-driven <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ballad_(music)" title="Ballad (music)">ballad</a> that contains a sample of the recording "Sabali" by the <a href="/wiki/Mali" title="Mali">Mali</a> musical duo <a href="/wiki/Amadou_%26_Mariam" title="Amadou &amp; Mariam">Amadou &amp; Mariam</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-idolator_41-0"><a href="#cite_note-idolator-41">[41]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Artwork">Artwork</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Overexposed_(album)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Artwork">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>On April 10, 2012, the band debuted the artwork of the album on their official website.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup> Created by the LA based art project <a href="/wiki/Young_%26_Sick" title="Young &amp; Sick">Young &amp; Sick</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-lostateminor_43-0"><a href="#cite_note-lostateminor-43">[43]</a></sup> the cover art doesn't feature any images of Maroon 5 and is instead a colorful collage of illustrations seemingly inspired by the likes of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Picasso" title="Picasso">Picasso</a> and a range of modern cartoonists.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup> According to Natalie Finn from <a href="/wiki/E!_News" title="E! News">E! News</a>, "the psychedelic <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Beatles" title="Beatles">Beatles</a>-dipped-in-Cream cover is a where-do-you-look-first wink at the pop-music world, which is so crowded with egos and images these days that it becomes almost impossible to just focus on the music."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-e.21_45-0"><a href="#cite_note-e.21-45">[45]</a></sup> Allison of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/MuchMusic" title="MuchMusic">MuchMusic</a> described the artwork as a combination of the 1967 album <i><a href="/wiki/Sgt._Pepper%27s_Lonely_Hearts_Club_Band" title="Sgt. Pepper's Lonely Hearts Club Band">Sgt. Pepper's Lonely Hearts Club Band</a></i> by <a href="/wiki/The_Beatles" title="The Beatles">The Beatles</a> and illustrations of American show <i><a href="/wiki/The_Simpsons" title="The Simpsons">The Simpsons</a></i>. The reviewer further noted that this is second time the band uses similar illustration the first one being on their 2002 debut album <i><a href="/wiki/Songs_About_Jane" title="Songs About Jane">Songs About Jane</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup> Jessica Sager from Pop Crush wrote, "the bright colors and cartoon images are representative of the album's themes."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup> Similarly, Rebecca Francois of Global Grind wrote that the artwork is like Maroon 5's music "fun and pop".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup> Becky Bain of website <a href="/wiki/Idolator_(website)" title="Idolator (website)">Idolator</a>, negatively reviewed the cover and wrote that "it is what an episode of <i>The Simpsons</i> looks like if you're on acid."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_49-0"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-49">[49]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Singles">Singles</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Overexposed_(album)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Singles">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>"Payphone" featuring Wiz Khalifa, was released as the <a href="/wiki/Lead_single" title="Lead single">lead single</a> from the album on April 17, 2012.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup> The song was received generally positive reviews from critics, they noted departure from older Maroon 5 songs. However, some them were praised of the music direction where the band has taken.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup> Magazine <i>Rolling Stone</i> placed "Payphone" at number 46 on their list of 50 Best Songs of 2012.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup> Commercially, the song reached number one on over <a href="/wiki/Payphone_(song)#Charts_and_certifications" title="Payphone (song)">eight national singles charts</a> and peaked within the top-ten on <a href="/wiki/Payphone_(song)#Charts_and_certifications" title="Payphone (song)">20 additional charts</a>. "Payphone" reached number two on the US <i>Billboard</i> Hot 100<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup> and number one on the <a href="/wiki/UK_Singles_Chart" title="UK Singles Chart">UK Singles Chart</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-digitalnews_54-0"><a href="#cite_note-digitalnews-54">[54]</a></sup> It was the fifth best selling single of 2012 with over 9.1 million digital copies sold worldwide.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Music_video" title="Music video">music video</a> of the song was directed by <a href="/wiki/Samuel_Bayer" title="Samuel Bayer">Samuel Bayer</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup> and features Levine being mistaken for a bank robber and fighting a fleet of policemen.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup></p>
<table class="mbox-small" role="presentation" style="border:1px solid #aaa;background-color:#f9f9f9;">

<div class="description" style="padding:2px 0 0 0"><a href="/wiki/Music_journalism" title="Music journalism">Music critics</a> praised the <a href="/wiki/Reggae" title="Reggae">reggae</a>-inspired composition and Levine's confident vocals on the song.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-omn_review_58-0"><a href="#cite_note-omn_review-58">[58]</a></sup></div>

<tr>
<td class="mbox-text" colspan="2" style="line-height:1.1em"><span><i>Problems playing this file? See <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Media_help" title="Wikipedia:Media help">media help</a>.</i></span></td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>"One More Night" was released as the second single from the album on June 19, 2012.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup> The song received generally positive reviews from critics who praised "the catchy reggae-drenched musical production" and "Adam Levine's confident pop vocals".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-omn_review_58-1"><a href="#cite_note-omn_review-58">[58]</a></sup> "One More Night" reached the top-ten on over <a href="/wiki/One_More_Night_(Maroon_5_song)#Weekly_charts" title="One More Night (Maroon 5 song)">26 national charts worldwide</a>. It topped the US <i>Billboard</i> Hot 100 for nine consecutive weeks becoming Maroon 5's longest topping single on the chart and was tied with "<a href="/wiki/Call_Me_Maybe" title="Call Me Maybe">Call Me Maybe</a>" by <a href="/wiki/Carly_Rae_Jepsen" title="Carly Rae Jepsen">Carly Rae Jepsen</a> for longest lead of the year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup> The music video of "One More Night" premiered on June 25, 2012 on <a href="/wiki/MTV" title="MTV">MTV</a> and was directed by <a href="/wiki/Peter_Berg" title="Peter Berg">Peter Berg</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup> The video features Levine's character being a boxer whose relationship is in ruins because of his profession, his love interest is played by American actress <a href="/wiki/Minka_Kelly" title="Minka Kelly">Minka Kelly</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup></p>
<p>"Daylight" was released as the third single from the album on November 27, 2012.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-daylight_release_64-0"><a href="#cite_note-daylight_release-64">[64]</a></sup> The song received generally mixed reviews from critics with Cameron Adams of <i><a href="/wiki/Herald_Sun" title="Herald Sun">Herald Sun</a></i> noting that "it sounds like Max Martin trying to write a Coldplay song by recycling his <a href="/wiki/Backstreet_Boys" title="Backstreet Boys">Backstreet Boys</a> handiwork."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-heraldsun_65-0"><a href="#cite_note-heraldsun-65">[65]</a></sup> "Daylight" reached the top-ten on over <a href="/wiki/Daylight_(Maroon_5_song)#Charts_and_certifications" title="Daylight (Maroon 5 song)">eight national charts worldwide</a> including number seven on the US <i>Billboard</i> Hot 100<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-billtop10_66-0"><a href="#cite_note-billtop10-66">[66]</a></sup> and number five on the <a href="/wiki/Canadian_Hot_100" title="Canadian Hot 100">Canadian Hot 100</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CAN_100_67-0"><a href="#cite_note-CAN_100-67">[67]</a></sup> Two music videos of the song are released: The first video "<a href="/wiki/Daylight_(Maroon_5_song)#Music_video" title="Daylight (Maroon 5 song)">The Daylight Project</a>", features hundred of fans and the people from around the world are connected to the song and the video was directed by <a href="/wiki/Jonas_%C3%85kerlund" title="Jonas Åkerlund">Jonas Åkerlund</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup> The second video "Playing for Change", includes several street musicians from around the world playing and sing along with the band on tour.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup></p>
<p>"Love Somebody" was released as the fourth and final single from the album on May 14, 2013.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LS_release_70-0"><a href="#cite_note-LS_release-70">[70]</a></sup> The song was received with mixed reviews from critics who praised the composition. However, the critical towards to Levine's vocals of the song.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ew_19-7"><a href="#cite_note-ew-19">[19]</a></sup> "Love Somebody" reached number 10 both on the Canadian Hot 100<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CAN_100_67-1"><a href="#cite_note-CAN_100-67">[67]</a></sup> and on the US <i>Billboard</i> Hot 100.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup> The band first performed the song during the fourth season of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Voice_(U.S._TV_series)" title="The Voice (U.S. TV series)">The Voice</a></i> on May 20, 2013. The official music video for the song, directed by <a href="/wiki/Rich_Lee" title="Rich Lee">Rich Lee</a>, was released the following day, on May 21, 2013. It features Levine, the other members of the band and Levine's love interest (played by model <a href="/wiki/Emily_Ratajkowski" title="Emily Ratajkowski">Emily Ratajkowski</a>) covered in paint.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Promotion_and_touring">Promotion and touring</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Overexposed_(album)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Promotion and touring">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Overexposed_Tour" title="Overexposed Tour">Overexposed Tour</a></div>
<p>To promote <i>Overexposed</i>, Maroon 5 played a concert at the <a href="/wiki/Ed_Sullivan_Theater" title="Ed Sullivan Theater">Ed Sullivan Theater</a> in New York on June 25, 2012, as part of the <i>Live on Letterman</i> concert series.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-davidletterman_73-0"><a href="#cite_note-davidletterman-73">[73]</a></sup> The band also performed "<a href="/wiki/Payphone_(song)" title="Payphone (song)">Payphone</a>" on the <i><a href="/wiki/Late_Show_with_David_Letterman" title="Late Show with David Letterman">Late Show with David Letterman</a></i> a day later. Levine gave an interview and performed "Payphone" with the band on <a href="/wiki/Late_Night_with_Jimmy_Fallon" title="Late Night with Jimmy Fallon">Late Night with Jimmy Fallon</a> on June 28, 2012.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup> The next day, Maroon 5 appeared on the <i><a href="/wiki/Today_(U.S._TV_program)" title="Today (U.S. TV program)">Today Show</a></i> (as part of the Toyota Summer Concert Series),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-today_75-0"><a href="#cite_note-today-75">[75]</a></sup> playing the hits: "<a href="/wiki/Payphone" title="Payphone">Payphone</a>", "<a href="/wiki/One_More_Night_(Maroon_5_song)" title="One More Night (Maroon 5 song)">One More Night</a>", "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Moves_Like_Jagger" title="Moves Like Jagger">Moves Like Jagger</a>" and "<a href="/wiki/Harder_to_Breathe" title="Harder to Breathe">Harder to Breathe</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-today_75-1"><a href="#cite_note-today-75">[75]</a></sup> The band started the "<a href="/wiki/Overexposed_Tour" title="Overexposed Tour">Overexposed Tour</a>" with 4 shows in <a href="/wiki/Mexico" title="Mexico">Mexico</a>, 3 of them sold out, with the first show being on August 14, 2012 in <a href="/wiki/Monterrey" title="Monterrey">Monterrey</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nuevo_Leon" title="Nuevo Leon">Nuevo Leon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mexico" title="Mexico">Mexico</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-shows_76-0"><a href="#cite_note-shows-76">[76]</a></sup> In August, they performed 3 shows in <a href="/wiki/Brazil" title="Brazil">Brazil</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-shows_76-1"><a href="#cite_note-shows-76">[76]</a></sup> and visited three other <a href="/wiki/South_America" title="South America">South American</a> countries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-shows_76-2"><a href="#cite_note-shows-76">[76]</a></sup> Through September and October, they visited many <a href="/wiki/East_Asia" title="East Asia">East Asian</a> countries, including: <a href="/wiki/South_Korea" title="South Korea">South Korea</a>, <a href="/wiki/Philippines" title="Philippines">Philippines</a>, <a href="/wiki/Malaysia" title="Malaysia">Malaysia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Singapore" title="Singapore">Singapore</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hong_Kong" title="Hong Kong">Hong Kong</a>, <a href="/wiki/Taiwan" title="Taiwan">Taiwan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Japan" title="Japan">Japan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Indonesia" title="Indonesia">Indonesia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Thailand" title="Thailand">Thailand</a>. The tour also included two shows in <a href="/wiki/Sydney" title="Sydney">Sydney</a> and <a href="/wiki/Melbourne" title="Melbourne">Melbourne</a>, <a href="/wiki/Australia" title="Australia">Australia</a> in October 2012. On September 7, 2012 <a href="/wiki/Adam_Levine" title="Adam Levine">Adam Levine</a> announced that the band would be extending the tour and play some more shows, starting in early 2013. Apparently, extra eight shows in Istanbul, Auckland, Bogota, Madrid, Warsaw, Caracas and Quito were planned, but this ultimately never came to fruition.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-digitalspyvid_77-0"><a href="#cite_note-digitalspyvid-77">[77]</a></sup> On October 22, 2012, Levine revealed the U.S. tour dates and stated that <a href="/wiki/Neon_Trees" title="Neon Trees">Neon Trees</a>, <a href="/wiki/Owl_City" title="Owl City">Owl City</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Kelly_Clarkson" title="Kelly Clarkson">Kelly Clarkson</a> will be supporting them throughout the U.S. tour.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-maroontourdaylight_78-0"><a href="#cite_note-maroontourdaylight-78">[78]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Critical_reception">Critical reception</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Overexposed_(album)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Critical reception">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<tr>
<td style="text-align:center;vertical-align:middle"><i><a href="/wiki/Spin_(magazine)" title="Spin (magazine)">Spin</a></i></td>
<td style="text-align:center;vertical-align:middle">4/10<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-spinreview_80-0"><a href="#cite_note-spinreview-80">[80]</a></sup></td>
</tr>
</table>
<p><i>Overexposed</i> received generally mixed reviews from <a href="/wiki/Music_journalism" title="Music journalism">music critics</a>. At <a href="/wiki/Metacritic" title="Metacritic">Metacritic</a>, which assigns a <a href="/wiki/Standard_score" title="Standard score">normalized</a> rating out of 100 to reviews from mainstream critics, the album received an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Weighted_mean" title="Weighted mean">average</a> score of 54, based on 14 reviews.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup> Evan Sawdey of <a href="/wiki/PopMatters" title="PopMatters">PopMatters</a> found it both interesting and flawed because of Maroon 5's attempt to pursue different ideas, which are ultimately unsuccessful.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-popmatters_79-1"><a href="#cite_note-popmatters-79">[79]</a></sup> Caroline Sullivan of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Guardian" title="The Guardian">The Guardian</a></i> said that the album lacks memorable hooks and "charm", despite Maroon 5's collaboration with popular producers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-guardian_24-2"><a href="#cite_note-guardian-24">[24]</a></sup> Adam Markowitz of <i><a href="/wiki/Entertainment_Weekly" title="Entertainment Weekly">Entertainment Weekly</a></i> felt that the lyrics are poorly written and that its production by several "pop kingpins" detracts from the band's performance, as the album does not consolidate its "rock grit and dance-pop glitz".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ew_19-9"><a href="#cite_note-ew-19">[19]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/MusicOMH" title="MusicOMH">musicOMH</a>'s Martyn Young wrote that Maroon 5's pop-produced direction exposes their limitations and lacks subtlety.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-musicOMH_22-4"><a href="#cite_note-musicOMH-22">[22]</a></sup> Andy Gill of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Independent" title="The Independent">The Independent</a></i> found the album dull, unimaginative, and marred by inarticulate "whoah-oh-oh" hooks.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-independent_36-2"><a href="#cite_note-independent-36">[36]</a></sup> Nick Levine of <i><a href="/wiki/NME" title="NME">NME</a></i> panned Adam Levine's singing and called him "the sort of chump who thinks that he's a 'player' but then goes and writes a song called 'Ladykiller' about, erm, a girl."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nmereview_30-4"><a href="#cite_note-nmereview-30">[30]</a></sup> Keith Harris of <i><a href="/wiki/Spin_(magazine)" title="Spin (magazine)">Spin</a></i> found the album middling with "plaintive vulnerability" that lacks both distractions and highlights.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-spinreview_80-1"><a href="#cite_note-spinreview-80">[80]</a></sup></p>
<p>In a positive review for <i><a href="/wiki/Rolling_Stone" title="Rolling Stone">Rolling Stone</a></i>, <a href="/wiki/Rob_Sheffield" title="Rob Sheffield">Rob Sheffield</a> called <i>Overexposed</i> the band's best album yet and said that its first-rate, dulcet sound is complemented by sharp, womanizing lyrics.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rollingstonereview_21-3"><a href="#cite_note-rollingstonereview-21">[21]</a></sup> Nate Chinen of <i><a href="/wiki/The_New_York_Times" title="The New York Times">The New York Times</a></i> felt that, although Levine sounds awkward when deviating from the slick style, the album further invests in their "glib" strengths, including Levine's supple voice.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Stephen_Thomas_Erlewine" title="Stephen Thomas Erlewine">Stephen Thomas Erlewine</a>, writing for <a href="/wiki/AllMusic" title="AllMusic">AllMusic</a>, said that the "briskly contemporary" album may not be as good as <i>Hands All Over</i>, but it will ensure the band's commercial momentum.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-allmusic_20-2"><a href="#cite_note-allmusic-20">[20]</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/American_Songwriter" title="American Songwriter">American Songwriter</a></i> magazine's Eric Allen believed that newer fans of the band from "today's beat oriented downloading musical culture" will be excited by <i>Overexposed</i>, although it may alienate their older fans and "music snobs".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-americansongwriter_17-2"><a href="#cite_note-americansongwriter-17">[17]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Commercial_performance">Commercial performance</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Overexposed_(album)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Commercial performance">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p><i>Overexposed</i> debuted at number 2 on the <a href="/wiki/Billboard_200" title="Billboard 200"><i>Billboard</i> 200</a>, behind <a href="/wiki/Linkin_Park" title="Linkin Park">Linkin Park</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/Living_Things_(Linkin_Park_album)" title="Living Things (Linkin Park album)">Living Things</a></i>, with sales of 222,000 copies, according to <a href="/wiki/Nielsen_SoundScan" title="Nielsen SoundScan">Nielsen SoundScan</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-billboarddebut_83-0"><a href="#cite_note-billboarddebut-83">[83]</a></sup> A little over 1,000 copies sold separates the two titles.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-billboarddebut_83-1"><a href="#cite_note-billboarddebut-83">[83]</a></sup> <i>Living Things</i> also kept the album from reaching number one in many other countries. <i>Overexposed</i> is the band's fourth studio album, and follows 2010's <i><a href="/wiki/Hands_All_Over_(album)" title="Hands All Over (album)">Hands All Over</a></i>, which also peaked at number 2, selling 142,000 in its first week.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-billboarddebut_83-2"><a href="#cite_note-billboarddebut-83">[83]</a></sup> <i>Overexposed</i>'s start marks the band's best sales week for an album since 2007's <i><a href="/wiki/It_Won%27t_Be_Soon_Before_Long" title="It Won't Be Soon Before Long">It Won't Be Soon Before Long</a></i> debuted at number one with 429,000 copies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-billboarddebut_83-3"><a href="#cite_note-billboarddebut-83">[83]</a></sup> In the second week, the album fell to number 4, with sales of 68,000 copies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Billboard200secondweek_84-0"><a href="#cite_note-Billboard200secondweek-84">[84]</a></sup> It felling out of top 10 in its seventh week, but the album rose to number 5, in its eight-week, as the album benefits from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Amazon_MP3" title="Amazon MP3">Amazon MP3</a> sale priced for $3.99 on August 17, 2012.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-billboard7week_85-0"><a href="#cite_note-billboard7week-85">[85]</a></sup> It sold 988,000 copies in the US in 2012, the 11th best-selling album of the year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-yahoo2012_86-0"><a href="#cite_note-yahoo2012-86">[86]</a></sup> As of August 2013, it has sold 1,431,000 copies in the US.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-yahoo2013_87-0"><a href="#cite_note-yahoo2013-87">[87]</a></sup></p>
<p>In Canada, the album debuted at number 3 on the <a href="/wiki/Canadian_Albums_Chart" title="Canadian Albums Chart">Canadian Albums Chart</a>, selling 17,800 copies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-canadianchart_88-0"><a href="#cite_note-canadianchart-88">[88]</a></sup> The album has sold 30,000 copies in <a href="/wiki/Brazil" title="Brazil">Brazil</a>, being certified <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gold_certification" title="Gold certification">Gold</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-brazilgold_89-0"><a href="#cite_note-brazilgold-89">[89]</a></sup> The album was certified Gold in <a href="/wiki/Japan" title="Japan">Japan</a> after selling 100,000+ copies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup> The album debuted at number 2 on the <a href="/wiki/UK_Albums_Chart" title="UK Albums Chart">UK Albums Chart</a>, selling 38,000 copies, becoming their third British bestseller.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ukdebut_91-0"><a href="#cite_note-ukdebut-91">[91]</a></sup> It was 3,000 copies behind of Linkin Park's <i>Living Things</i>, which debuted at number one with 41,000 copies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ukdebut_91-1"><a href="#cite_note-ukdebut-91">[91]</a></sup> The album sold 263,000 copies in 2012 in the UK.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Track_listings">Track listings</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Overexposed_(album)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Track listings">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<dl>
<dt>Notes</dt>
</dl>
<ul>
<li><sup><span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_a"><b><a href="#ref_a">^a</a></b></span></sup> signifies an additional <a href="/wiki/Record_producer" title="Record producer">producer</a></li>
<li><sup><span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_b"><b><a href="#ref_b">^b</a></b></span></sup> signifies a co-<a href="/wiki/Record_producer" title="Record producer">producer</a></li>
<li>"Wipe Your Eyes" contains a sample of the recording "Sabali", written by <a href="/wiki/Damon_Albarn" title="Damon Albarn">Damon Albarn</a>, <a href="/wiki/Amadou_%26_Mariam" title="Amadou &amp; Mariam">Mariam Doumbia</a> and Marc Moreau, and performed by <a href="/wiki/Amadou_%26_Mariam" title="Amadou &amp; Mariam">Amadou &amp; Mariam</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-credits_95-0"><a href="#cite_note-credits-95">[95]</a></sup></li>
<li>"Wasted Years" contains samples of "The Rill Thing", written and performed by <a href="/wiki/Little_Richard" title="Little Richard">"Little" Richard Penniman</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-credits_95-1"><a href="#cite_note-credits-95">[95]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Personnel">Personnel</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Overexposed_(album)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Personnel">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<dl>
<dt>Maroon 5</dt>
</dl>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Adam_Levine" title="Adam Levine">Adam Levine</a> – lead and backing vocals, rhythm guitar, songwriting, production</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Mickey_Madden" title="Mickey Madden">Mickey Madden</a> – bass guitar, songwriting, backing vocals</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/James_Valentine_(musician)" title="James Valentine (musician)">James Valentine</a> – lead and rhythm guitar, backing vocals, sitar, keyboards, songwriting, production</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Matt_Flynn_(musician)" title="Matt Flynn (musician)">Matt Flynn</a> – drums, percussion</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/PJ_Morton" title="PJ Morton">PJ Morton</a> – keyboards, synthesizers, backing vocals</li>
</ul>
<dl>
<dt>Additional musicians</dt>
</dl>
<ul>
<li>Dan Omelio – guitars, keyboards, synthesizers, songwriting, production</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Benny_Blanco" title="Benny Blanco">Benny Blanco</a> – guitars, keyboards, synthesizers, songwriting, production</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Shellback_(record_producer)" title="Shellback (record producer)">Shellback</a> – production, songwriting, guitars, keyboards, synthesizers, programming, drums, backing vocals</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Max_Martin" title="Max Martin">Max Martin</a> – backing vocals, guitars, keyboards, songwriting, production</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Ammar_Malik" title="Ammar Malik">Ammar Malik</a> – backing vocals, guitars, songwriting</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Wiz_Khalifa" title="Wiz Khalifa">Wiz Khalifa</a> – rap (featured guest on "<a href="/wiki/Payphone_(song)" title="Payphone (song)">Payphone</a>")</li>
<li>Brie Larson – backing vocals</li>
<li>Savannah Buffet – backing vocals</li>
<li>Dan Keyes – backing vocals</li>
<li>Z. Berg – backing vocals</li>
<li>Vanessa Long – backing vocals</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Sam_Farrar" title="Sam Farrar">Sam Farrar</a> – production, programming, backing vocals</li>
<li>MdL – keyboards, drums, production</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Ryan_Tedder" title="Ryan Tedder">Ryan Tedder</a> – keyboards, songwriting, production</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Noel_Zancanella" title="Noel Zancanella">Noel Zancanella</a> – keyboards, songwriting, production</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Brian_West_(musician)" title="Brian West (musician)">Brian "Sweetwesty" West</a> – guitar, programming, songwriting, production</li>
<li>Noah "Mailbox" Passovoy – production, keyboards</li>
<li>David Silberstein – wine glasses</li>
<li>Scott Yarmovsky – wine glasses</li>
</ul>
<p>Based on the liner notes of <i>Overexposed</i>, A&amp;M/Octone Records.</p>
